## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lone canonical row cannot express this theme's real structure, a mirrored text with a canonical origin, the rust-coder-02 copy holds editorial authority because its bundle authored the doctrine, this copy holds habitat authority for how the executable-specs bundle consumes it, and neither copy outranks the other on content because content is provably identical
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because authority follows authorship for text and follows habitat for usage, so the hierarchy splits by question type rather than by file, an arrangement single-copy themes never need
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: content disputes settled against this copy invite fork pressure, each local ruling is one temptation to annotate the local text, while usage disputes settled at the origin import workflow assumptions from a bundle the asker is not in

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic worked-example artifact misses this theme's natural object, a mirror ledger, one standing record holding the pair of paths, the latest diff result with its date, the routing dependencies that break on divergence, the host router's section references into this file, and the upstream-first maintenance rule for edits
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every obligation this theme created, fork detection, dispatch integrity, delegation of freshness, reads from the same small fact set, so one artifact holding those facts serves all the probes instead of each rediscovering them
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: without the ledger, each audit re-derives the pair relationship from scratch, and the first maintainer who does not know the second copy exists edits confidently, the fork arriving through ignorance rather than intent
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: one ledger per mirrored pair, gate records belong to the gates theme and routing manifests to the reference-maps theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the artifact as the mirror ledger with five fields, paths, dated diff, dependent routers, section references, maintenance rule, refreshed each audit cycle

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed symbol-count boundary misprices mirror work, whose units are per-audit relational cost, the diff, the grep, and the ledger refresh, per-maintenance-event cost, the upstream-first flow with re-mirroring, and per-consultation cost, which this theme adds nothing to because consumption effort belongs to the doctrine and the router
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the theme's own work is pure metadata upkeep, minutes per audit cycle and a bounded flow per rare edit, so its workload rounds to near-zero between events, the cheapest theme in the cluster to keep healthy
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the mispricing risk runs opposite to most themes, this work is so cheap it gets skipped as trivial, and skipped relational audits are how forks and rot accumulate their silent quarters
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: budgeting this theme's mirror obligations, consumption and implementation workload belong to the doctrine and routing themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the model in its three units and their expected magnitudes, minutes per audit, one bounded flow per edit event, zero marginal consultation cost
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that cheap standing obligations survive best when attached to expensive ones, the relational audit should ride the corpus's existing reread cadence rather than owning a schedule, because a task too small to schedule is a task that silently stops, piggybacking is the survival strategy for near-zero workloads

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the layers fail independently and mislead differently, unobservable code hides runtime failures from operators, an unobservable mirror hides corpus failures from maintainers, and only the second is this theme's to fix
